### Question 1: I am writing to request your review of my course tracking in preparation for graduation. I am pursuing a double major in Computer Science and Applied Mathematics. I have attached the spreadsheet tracking my courses for your review. I would appreciate it if you could take a look and provide any necessary feedback: Humility, Global Humanities and Social Change, Linear Algebra, Modern Vietnamese Culture and Society, Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age, Discrete Math, Computer Science II: Data Structures, Programming for Data Science and Visualization, Design and Systems Thinking, Scientific Inquiry, Computer Organization, Calculus, Intelligent Robot Studio: From Theory to Practice, How to become a writer: lessons from Vietnamese and non-Vietnamese writers, Introduction to Political Science, The Global Vietnam War II, Deep Learning for Artificial Intelligence, Advanced Deep Learning, Probability, Computer Science I: Introduction to Programming, Algorithms and Theory of Computing, Database System, Advanced Programming Techniques, Introduction to Artificial Intelligence, Machine Learning for Data Science, Multivariable Calculus, Mathematical Statistics, General Work Program (GWP) 1, [Independent Research Project] Labeled FreSCo- Mining Frequent Patterns in labeled Simplicial Complexes, Object-Oriented Analysis and Design, Statistical Learning, Operating Systems, Abstract Algebra, Differential Equations, Stochastic Calculus, Natural Language Processing, Advanced Linear Algebra.  
### Answer: 

Based on the course list you have provided, it appears that you are on track to complete the requirements for both your Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors.

For the Computer Science major, you have completed or are enrolled in the following required courses: Computer Science I: Introduction to Programming, Algorithms and Theory of Computing, Computer Science II: Data Structures, Computer Organization, Operating Systems, Database System, Advanced Programming Techniques, Object-Oriented Analysis and Design, and Natural Language Processing. You also have elective courses such as Intelligent Robot Studio: From Theory to Practice, Deep Learning for Artificial Intelligence, Advanced Deep Learning, and Machine Learning for Data Science.

For the Applied Mathematics major, you have completed or are enrolled in the following required courses: Linear Algebra, Calculus, Multivariable Calculus, Mathematical Statistics, Probability, and Advanced Linear Algebra. You also have elective courses such as Differential Equations, Stochastic Calculus, and Abstract Algebra.

In addition, you have completed or are enrolled in the following core courses: Humility, Global Humanities and Social Change, Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age, Scientific Inquiry, Design and Systems Thinking, and General Work Program (GWP) 1. You also have elective courses such as Modern Vietnamese Culture and Society, Introduction to Political Science, The Global Vietnam War II, and [Independent Research Project] Labeled FreSCo- Mining Frequent Patterns in labeled Simplicial Complexes.

It is important to note that you also need to complete the required courses in the QUEST (Quantitative Understanding and Empirical Scientific Thinking) core group, which includes Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age, Scientific Inquiry, Introduction to Statistics, and Programming for Data Science and Visualization. These courses are pre-assigned to students in their first year or the first semester of the second year.

Overall, it appears that you are on track to complete the degree requirements for both your Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors. I would recommend double-checking your progress in the QUEST core group and ensuring that you have fulfilled all the institutional requirements for graduation. If you have any questions or concerns, please let me know.

### Question 2: Can you differentiate a cross-listed course and elective applied course in the case of a double major?  
### Answer: 

In the context provided, a cross-listed course is a course that is offered under multiple majors or minors and can be used to satisfy requirements for more than one major or minor. On the other hand, an elective applied course is a course from another major that emphasizes the applications of Mathematics. A student must take at least 2 applied courses (at least one at 200 level) as part of their Mathematics major requirements. However, if a cross-listed course is also an applied course, it can be used to satisfy both the applied course requirement and the requirements for one or more majors or minors, up to a limit of 8 credits (two courses) per pair of majors or major and minor. It's important to note that this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged.  

<details>

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can

### Question 3: I would like to ask for the capstone withdrawal policy. What will be the impact when I choose to drop the capstone before the Fall 2025 term starts? Will there be any penalties associated with withdrawing, such as a 'W' notation on my transcript?  
### Answer: 

The capstone withdrawal policy is not explicitly mentioned in the provided context. However, based on the information given about the Course Withdrawal policy, if you withdraw from the capstone before the Fall 2025 term starts during the first withdrawal period (Week 2 to Week 4), there will be no consequences in your Academic Records, and no 'W' notation will be recorded on your transcript. If you withdraw during the second withdrawal period (Week 4 to Week 8), a 'W' grade will be recorded, but it will not affect your GPA. Keep in mind that you should consult with your Academic/Major Advisor before making a decision to withdraw from the capstone. For more specific details about the capstone withdrawal policy, you may need to refer to your program's academic regulations or consult with your academic advisor.

The first period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4. During this time, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. ### Question 4: Questions related to course history, in which one course can have multiple IDs? Like Advanced Deep Learning course. How would it be handled among different cohorts?  
### Answer: 

In the context provided, the Advanced Deep Learning course (CS311) is listed under multiple IDs such as CS311, CS310, and CS313. This suggests that the course may have been offered under different IDs in different semesters or cohorts. However, without specific information about the course numbering system and the university's policies regarding course number changes, it's difficult to determine the exact handling of such situations. It's possible that the course content remains the same but is taught by different instructors or under different names, or that the course content evolves over time and is renumbered accordingly. It's also possible that the course is offered under multiple IDs simultaneously, catering to students with different prerequisites or interests. Without more context, it's impossible to say for certain.

### Question 5: I have taken Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis in Fall 2023. Am I eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you are eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024. According to the course electives mapping, students should complete all of the Intermediate level courses (which include Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis) by the end of their third year before taking Advanced level courses. Therefore, you have met the prerequisites to take Financial Economics, which is an Advanced level course. However, it is always a good idea to check with the Economics major coordinator to confirm your eligibility.

Courses: Principles of Economics 1 and 2 (100-level) These two courses introduce microeconomics and macroeconomics, providing an overview of economic theories and analytical techniques applied to current issues. By studying both microeconomics (the analysis of choices made by people, firms, and governments) and macroeconomics (the analysis of the economy as a whole) students will develop their economic intuition as they better understand the functioning of the world. Methodology Courses: Economic Methods (100-level) This course introduces basic concepts and methods of statistical analysis and fundamental rules of mathematics used in economic analysis. Students will be exposed to a wide range of economic problems and the methods to solve them. By completing this course, students will be qualified to take upper-level courses in the Economics major. ### Question 6: If I have waived the course Computer Science I, but I want to declare Computer Science major, do I have to take Computer Science I?  
### Answer: 

Yes, to formally declare Computer Science as your major, you must complete at least two Computer Science courses. Since Computer Science I is one of the required courses, you will need to take it or another equivalent course to fulfill this requirement.

### Question 7: If I have taken the following courses: Mathematical Statistics, Abstract Algebra, Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, Calculus, Differential Equation, Stochastic Calculus, Statistical Learning, Discrete Mathematics, Probability, am I eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics? What about majoring in Applied Mathematics?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you are eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics. You have taken at least 1 Advanced course (Stochastic Calculus) and 2 Intermediate courses (Discrete Mathematics, Probability). However, to major in Applied Mathematics, you need to complete at least 2 Foundation courses or 1 Foundation and 1 Intermediate courses. Since you have not mentioned taking any Foundation courses, you are not yet eligible to major in Applied Mathematics.

### Question 9: Is it possible that I write a book as my History Capstone?  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is possible to write a book as your History Capstone project. While the traditional format is a written thesis, the History Capstone project allows for alternative formats, including a book. However, it's important to note that the book should have a substantial written component and be based on primary source evidence. It's recommended to discuss your idea with your primary advisor to ensure it aligns with the project's objectives and your career goals.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
and provide constructive feedback at the defense. ● Serve as a second reader and evaluator for your final project. 1.6. Project Format There is no specific format requirement for the History Capstone project. Most students choose to write a traditional thesis (as of Fall 2024, all the History Capstone projects have adopted this format), but students are free to adopt other formats as well. Suggested alternative formats may include: ● a short documentary film, ● a podcast, ● a historical exhibition, or ● an interactive digital narrative. Students who expect to apply to postgraduate schools or enter writing-intensive careers after graduation may benefit most from the experience of authoring a written thesis based on archival materials or other primary sources (including oral history interviews), which they can furnish as a writing sample or use as the basis for a graduate thesis. But students who wish to pursue other careers may find that an alternative format is the best option: for example, a Tip: Your

### Question 10: Given I have finished these subjects: Advanced Deep Learning, Machine Learning, Deep Learning, Database. Are they sufficient for the Advanced Courses requirement of the computer science major?  
### Answer: 

Yes, the subjects you have mentioned (Advanced Deep Learning, Machine Learning, Deep Learning, Database) are sufficient for the Advanced Courses requirement of the computer science major, as they cover the topics of deep learning, machine learning, and databases, which are typically required for advanced courses in computer science. However, it is always a good idea to check the specific requirements of your university or program to ensure that you meet all the necessary prerequisites for the advanced courses you are interested in.

### Question 11: I have a question if I take a gap year, will my financial aid be canceled? If yes, can I still re-apply for the financial aid program when I get back to school?  
### Answer: 

If you take a gap year, your enrollment in the program will be canceled, but you can still re-apply for financial aid when you get back to school by re-applying for admission and financial aid. However, the academic regulations, degree program, and curriculum requirements in effect at the time of readmission will apply to you.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
student must meet with the Dean’s Office, who establishes the conditions that the student must meet prior to returning to Fulbright. While on suspension, a student may not visit the Fulbright campus unless permission is given from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions typically are for one term or one academic year. A student may be suspended a maximum of two times. A student will not be suspended a third time but will instead have their enrolment in the program canceled. A student in this situation must apply for re-admission. The student must include with his or her application for re-admission a letter that addresses the reasons for their suspensions and cancellation, and the measures they have taken to address those reasons. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. Students who are re-admitted must also re- apply for financial aid.

Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. ### Question 12: I am aware that Fulbright has to organize online classes instead of on-campus ones. Therefore, will there be any change in the tuition fee?  
### Answer: 

The text does not provide information about any changes in tuition fees due to online classes. However, it does mention that tuition credit may be considered in exceptional circumstances, as per the "Fees & Charges Guide" for undergraduate students. But this is not related to the mode of instruction (online or on-campus).  

<details>

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits.  Students should be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if resulting in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. • Waitlist: Each course at Fulbright has a maximum capacity. registration, is the process of formally recording the enrollment of a student in a course by the Office of the Registrar. The registration process validates the student’s intent to participate in courses for each term of the academic year.  Students cannot register for courses in the forthcoming term if they are not in “Active” status and/or have an outstanding financial balance on their account. 3.3 Course Change/Add/Drop and Waitlist Policies All courses offered at Fulbright follow the same course change/add/drop/ and withdrawal timeline. • Course Change/Add/Drop: The Add/Drop period lasts for two weeks from the start of each term, from the beginning of Week 1 to 4:00 PM on Friday of Week 2. Students can freely add/drop course(s) during this time, except the Core courses. In addition, students should be aware that changes are subject to space limitations, and students are responsible for

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
account. 3.3 Course Change/Add/Drop and Waitlist Policies All courses offered at Fulbright follow the same course change/add/drop/ and withdrawal timeline. • Course Change/Add/Drop: The Add/Drop period lasts for two weeks from the start of each term, from the beginning of Week 1 to 4:00 PM on Friday of Week 2. Students can freely add/drop course(s) during this time, except the Core courses. In addition, students should be aware that changes are subject to space limitations, and students are responsible for maintaining the full-time enrollment status of registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. • Course Withdrawal: There are two Withdrawal periods per term. The first period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4. During this time, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. Attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which  

</details> 

### Question 13: If I major in Economics, is it sufficient that I take Scholar Development to fulfill Experiential Learning requirements?  
### Answer: 

No, while Scholar Development is a valuable course, it does not necessarily fulfill the Experiential Learning requirements for the Economics major. To fulfill these requirements, you must complete at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under Fulbright's Experiential Learning Program (ELP), which can be housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), or the Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation. It is essential to consult with your advisor to ensure that the experiential learning experiences you choose will count toward your major requirements.

### Question 14: Is it sufficient for me to complete 4 credits in EL if I major in Engineering?  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is sufficient for you to complete 4 credits in Experiential Learning (EL) if you major in Engineering, as per the degree requirements. However, at least one of these credits must be in Scholar Development, which must be approved by the Chair of Engineering.

### Question 15: Can I take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses, as long as you meet the prerequisites for the intermediate courses. However, to earn a bachelor's degree in engineering, you would need to take at least three engineering major courses at the 300-level or Advanced level, which includes the Capstone project.

Students interested in exploring further can take several Foundation Engineering courses, which are designed specifically to bridge engineering practice, mathematics, and basic sciences. In general, these courses only require the core engineering course as the prerequisite, if any, making them accessible to undetermined-major students to pursue courses of interest. Once the students declare their major or minor in Engineering, they will gain more specialized knowledge and skills by taking more Engineering Foundation courses and Engineering Advanced courses. As part of a human-centered approach that aims to determine human-centric problems and then apply innovative engineering solutions, the students will be encouraged to take Elective courses in Arts, Humanities, Social Sciences, and Entrepreneurship. ### Question 16: If I have completed the course Intro to AI, will CS207 - Object-Oriented Analysis and Design and CS211 – Operating Systems suffice to fill the rest two intermediate courses?  
### Answer: 

Yes, if you have completed the course Intro to AI, then CS207 - Object-Oriented Analysis and Design and CS211 – Operating Systems would suffice to fill the rest two intermediate courses for the Computer Science major, as they are both intermediate level courses. However, to formally declare Computer Science as your major, you must complete at least two Computer Science courses, and MATH 202 - Discrete Math is also counted as one of them.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 19]
(AI) is a research ﬁeld that studies how to realize the intelligent human behaviors on a computer. The ultimate goal of AI is to make a computer that can learn, plan, and solve problems autonomously. In this course, student will learn the foundational principles and practice implementing some of these applications including representation, problem solving, and learning methods of artiﬁcial intelligence. Accordingly, students should be able to develop intelligent systems by assembling solutions to concrete computational problems; understand the role of knowledge representation, problem solving, and learning in intelligent-system engineering; and appreciate the role of problem solving, vision, and language in understanding human intelligence from a computational perspective. Topics covered in this course include class, object, information hiding, encapsulation, inheritance, interface, polymorphism, design patterns, multi-threading, database connection, unit testing, and Uniﬁed Modeling Language (UML). Students will work in teams to practice designing software using UML models such as use-case, sequence, and class diagrams. ### Question 17: Does completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfy the core theory requirement, or is an additional course needed?  
### Answer: 

Completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfies the core theory requirement for the Economics major. The core theory requirement includes Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis, and these two courses are covered by Microeconomics and Macroeconomics respectively. No additional course is needed to meet this requirement.

### Question 18: If I want to major in Engineering, can I choose other programming courses besides Computer Science I and Computer Science II, for instance Introduction to data visualization?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can choose other programming courses such as Introduction to Data Visualization, as long as they fit into your major requirements and help you meet the Program Learning Outcomes (PLOs). However, Computer Science I and Computer Science II are typically fundamental courses in a Computer Science major, so they are often recommended.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 19]
Prerequisites: None (CS104 is recommended) This course aims to equip students with the skills necessary to solve computational problems using a high-level programming language. Students will develop their abilities to use (i) fundamental programming constructs such as branching statements, loops, functions, and recursion and (ii) abstract data types such as lists and maps. Students will also be exposed to basic concepts of object-oriented programming. The course demonstrates data visualization by understanding, questioning, and problematizing how data are generated, analyzed, and used. The students will be able to apply concepts and skills to visualize data, interpret the ﬁndings, and examine the impacts of data-driven decision. The course will also get the students familiar

### Question 19: Given I took Discrete Mathematics in Spring 2022 and earned B, then the same course in Spring 2024 and earned C-, which grades will be kept?  
### Answer: 

In this scenario, the higher grade (B) will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade (C-) will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. The credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. However, a student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. It is recommended to consult with the Academic/Major Advisor about the program plan if considering taking the class for a third time.

### Question 20: Can I register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4?  
### Answer: 

No, the exploratory courses E4 are for Mathematics and Computing at the 100-level or 200-level. 300-level math courses do not fall under this category.

### Question 21: Can I register for more than 20 credits in a semester?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can register for a maximum of 20 credits per term, but you need to complete the Request for Maximum Course Load per Term form and get the Academic Advisor's approval. The form should be submitted to the Office of the Registrar before the end date of the online registration period.

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. ### Question 22: What is the maximum number of times I can retake a course to improve my grade, and how does it affect my transcript?  
### Answer: 

You can retake a course twice to improve your grade. If you retake a course and get a higher grade, the higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. However, you cannot retake the same course for the third time unless you failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. The credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits.

The first period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4. During this time, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. Attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. ### Question 23: For a student doing the literature capstone, if a student includes charts or tables, do they count toward the word limit?  
### Answer: 

The provided guidelines do not mention charts or tables in relation to the word limit. However, since images with captions are not included in the word count, it is possible that charts or tables might also not be included in the word count. It would be best to clarify this with the specific guidelines or the instructor of the course.

### Question 24: If I failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, can I redo it in Spring 2025?  
### Answer: 

Yes, if you failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, you can redo it in Spring 2025. However, you should note that you must have no outstanding Incompletes at the time of application and maintain a 3.2 GPA throughout your senior year to be able to earn an Honors for the Capstone. Failure to maintain the required GPA will result in the Capstone being capped at Pass. Also, the approximate timeline suggests that you should submit your Capstone Proposal form in the Spring semester before your Capstone year, and submit your Capstone I portfolio to your primary and secondary advisors by the last day of the Capstone I semester. Therefore, it is important to follow the timeline and the requirements to ensure a successful redemption of Capstone I.

### Question 25: If I do Literature capstone in Decolonial studies, can it be approved?  
### Answer: 

Yes, it can be approved if there is a faculty member in Literature who has expertise in Decolonial studies. However, it is important to consult with the prospective advisor early in junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of the proposed project. If there is no faculty expertise in Decolonial studies, the project may not be approved.

### Question 26: I am a Co24 majoring in Computer Science and taking the Database course. Does it count as major courses?  
### Answer: 

Yes, the Database course (CS304) is considered an advanced course in the Computer Science major, so it does count towards the major requirements.

### Question 27: Can Discrete Mathematics be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors?  
### Answer: 

Yes, Discrete Mathematics (MATH 202) can be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors. It is a requirement for the Computer Science major and can also be used to fulfill the required foundation courses for the Applied Mathematics major.

### Question 28: What steps should I take to ensure a smooth transfer of my exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

To ensure a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright, you should follow these steps:

1. Read the Transfer Credit Policy V1.0 published in the One-Stop portal to understand the process and requirements.

2. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer. This can be found on the One-Stop portal.

3. Provide all the necessary information about the course(s) for which you are applying to transfer. This may include course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

4. Send an official transcript with seal from Bard College directly to the Office of the Registrar at Fulbright University Vietnam. You can send it via email to registrar@fulbright.edu.vn or by mail to the address provided in the Transfer Credit Policy.

5. After submitting your application, the Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

6. Note that Fulbright will not evaluate transferable credit prior to your acceptance. Transferable credit is determined after you enroll.

7. For more detailed information, refer to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development) and the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
their Fulbright undergraduate degree. This is referred to as Credit Transfer. In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar.

### Question 29: Are 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement?  
### Answer: 

Yes, courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 are also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement. Only courses from the specified categories (E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing) can be taken to fulfill the Exploratory requirement.

### Question 30: I am a Co25 student pursuing a Computer Science major, can I choose to follow either the old flowchart or the new one?  
### Answer: 

As a Co25 student, you are following the new flowchart for the Computer Science major. The new flowchart includes foundation, intermediate, and advanced courses, as well as the option to choose a concentration. However, you still have some flexibility in your choice of elective courses to explore your areas of interest deeper. If you have any specific questions about the courses or the flowchart, it would be best to consult with an academic advisor.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 12]

Following the completion of their foundation and intermediate courses, students will have ﬂexibility in their choice of four elective advanced courses to explore their areas of interest deeper. Finally, in the fourth year, students can choose to do the capstone to graduate with honors or to take two more intermediate or advanced courses to graduate without honors. ### Question 31: If I withdraw from a course after the 4th week of the semester, will I be deducted 4 credits of financial aid?  
### Answer: 

No, withdrawing from a course after the 4th week of the semester will not result in a deduction of 4 credits of financial aid. However, you will receive a grade of 'F' which may affect your GPA, and you will not be eligible for tuition credit unless there are exceptional circumstances. The attempted credits will be recorded on your transcript, but it will not affect your full-time enrollment status as long as you are registered for a minimum of 12 credits per term.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. Exceptions will only be permitted in exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. ### Question 32: Why do I need to take 8 exploratory courses?  
### Answer: 

You need to take 8 exploratory courses to step out of your comfort zone, explore broad areas of study, and discover more fully where your interests and passions lie. These courses are chosen from each of the three categories: Arts and Humanities, Social Sciences, and STEM. The number of exploratory courses varies depending on the class year, with Class of 2024 students needing to complete 16 credits (4 courses) and students of classes 2025, 2026, and 2027 needing to complete 32 credits (8 courses). Up to two of these exploratory courses can be counted towards your major requirements.  

<details>

These courses are pre-assigned to students in their first year or the first semester of the second year. ### Question 33: Can I take 160 credits in 4 years given that I pay for the full tuition fee?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take 160 credits in 4 years. The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. This means that in 4 years, you can take a maximum of 160 credit hours if you take the maximum course load every term. However, to graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours. Therefore, taking 160 credits in 4 years would exceed the minimum requirement and would not be beneficial.

### Question 34: What are the requirements for mathematics courses to pursue Human-Centered Engineering major?  
### Answer: 

The Human-Centered Engineering curriculum at Fulbright University Vietnam does not specify any particular requirements for mathematics courses. However, students are expected to have a core engineering course as a prerequisite for Foundation Engineering courses, which are designed to bridge engineering practice, mathematics, and basic sciences. These Foundation Engineering courses are accessible to undetermined-major students to pursue courses of interest. Once students declare their major or minor in Engineering, they will gain more specialized knowledge and skills by taking more Engineering Foundation courses and Engineering Advanced courses.

An ability to apply engineering design to produce solutions that meet specified needs with consideration of public health, safety, and welfare, as well as global, cultural, social, environmental, and economic factors (LO2), 3. ### Question 35: How is the grade of a replaced course displayed on the transcript? Will it replace the old one or create a new entry in the transcript?  
### Answer: 

The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. The higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The repeated course credits are counted toward the total attempted credits.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. ### Question 36: What are the courses that can replace the capstone for a given major?  
### Answer: 

If a student chooses not to do a capstone, they could replace it with 8 credits from courses within their major, including at least 4 credits of 300-level course(s). The specific courses that can replace the capstone may vary depending on the major. Students should discuss their proposals with program coordinators and advisors to determine the suitability and feasibility of their proposed course replacements.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Art & Media Studies Capstone Handbook _v3_210125.pdf, Page: 6]
1. General Information: A culmination to the student’s curriculum, the capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. The capstone may also draw from relevant extra-curricular activities and practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. The capstone should evidence competency in a primary disciplinary specialization (optionally supported by secondary and tertiary disciplinary areas). In the Art & Media Studies major, the capstone could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. For other kinds of projects, please consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project. Remember, the capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. However, it should not require extensive fieldwork. You should think very carefully about an

### Question 37: Is it possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics? If yes, please provide a sample study plan.  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics. However, the specific study plan may vary depending on the university's policies and the availability of courses. Here is a sample study plan based on the information provided in the context:

1. General education courses (Core and Exploratory, as required by Undergraduate curriculum), of which up to two Exploratory courses (8 credits) can be counted towards the major.
2. Experiential Learning (4 – 12 credits).
3. Required foundation courses for Human-Centered Engineering: Engineering Mathematics, Engineering Physics, Engineering Statistics, and Engineering Graphics (16 credits).
4. Required foundation courses for Applied Mathematics: Linear Algebra, Calculus, Introduction to Statistics, Multivariable Calculus (16 credits).
5. 1 writing course (Ideas in Mathematics/Advanced Mathematical Writing) (4 credits) for Applied Mathematics.
6. 2 intermediate courses (8 credits) for Human-Centered Engineering.
7. 1 Pure Mathematics course (4 credits) for Applied Mathematics.
8. 2 advanced courses in specialized areas of study for Applied Mathematics (8 credits).
9. 2 elective applied courses approved by the major coordinator (at least one at 200 level) (8 credits) for Applied Mathematics.
10. Research seminar (4 credits) for Applied Mathematics.
11. Capstone I and Capstone II (8 credits) for Human-Centered Engineering.
12. Additional elective courses from both Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics to meet the total credit requirement for graduation.

This study plan assumes that some courses may overlap between the two majors, and the student would need to choose elective courses carefully to ensure they meet the requirements for both majors. It is essential to consult with the academic advisors from both departments to create a personalized study plan.

### Question 39: What are the exchange policies of Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

At Fulbright, the course change/add/drop and withdrawal timeline is the same for all courses. During the Add/Drop period, which lasts for two weeks from the start of each term, students can freely add/drop course(s) except for Core courses. Changes are subject to space limitations, and students are responsible for maintaining the full-time enrollment status of registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. There are two Withdrawal periods per term. During the first period, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period allows students to withdraw from the course, but a "W" grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which they withdraw. In exceptional circumstances, students may request a tuition credit, but this requires supporting documentation and the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. Waitlisting is also available for courses that are full, and students will be enrolled in the course in order of their appearance on the waitlist during the registration or Add/Drop time.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits.  Students should be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if resulting in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. • Waitlist: Each course at Fulbright has a maximum capacity. The registration system on the Fulbright One Stop portal allows students to join a waitlist for courses that are full. Should space become available, students will be enrolled in the course in order of their appearance on the waitlist during the registration or Add/Drop time. ### Question 40: What actions are considered plagiarism? Are AI-generated works counted?  
### Answer: 

According to Fulbright University Vietnam's Code of Academic Integrity, plagiarism includes but is not limited to:

1. Submitting work that is not one's own, either in whole or in part, without proper citation.
2. Using someone else's ideas, words, or work without giving appropriate credit.
3. Representing someone else's work as one's own.
4. Submitting work that has been previously submitted for another course without the instructor's permission.

Regarding AI-generated works, the Code of Academic Integrity states that creative projects involving generative AI will require full documentation of its usage. This means that if AI is used to generate any part of a project, it must be clearly documented, and the originality and human contributions to the project must be highlighted. If the AI-generated work is not properly documented and the human contributions are not clearly defined, it could be considered plagiarism.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]
approval process can be found at https://fulbright.edu.vn/irb/ 1.7. Academic Integrity The Capstone is subject to the regulations described in Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity, including updates on usage of generative AI. Creative projects involving generative AI will require full documentation of its usage. Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include: • Objective and Scope: Clearly deﬁne the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the speciﬁc elements of the project it contributes to. • Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed. • Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI. • Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout

### Question 41: Why is the graduation requirement 128 credits, but the major requirement is only 48 credits?  
### Answer: 

The graduation requirement is 128 credits because students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue to explore different subjects across the curriculum, build a broad and diverse background, or pursue more specialized studies within their major. The major requirement is only 48 credits because it includes specific courses required for the major, such as Introduction to Programming, Data Structures & Algorithms, and Computer Organization, among others.

### Question 42: Explain the cross-listed mechanism between courses.  
### Answer: 

In the context provided, cross-listed courses are courses that can be counted towards the requirements of more than one major or minor. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C, and if there are cross-listed courses between A and B, B and C, and A and C, the student can use up to 6 of these courses to satisfy the requirements of all three areas of study. The limit is 8 credits (two courses) per each pair of majors (or major and minor), and this limit does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. However, this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed. Additionally, this mechanism does not apply to courses that are required for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major if these courses are not cross-listed between the majors. In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors, which are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. ### Question 43: When is the graduation ceremony for Co25?  
### Answer: 

The question does not provide information about the graduation ceremony for Class of 2025. However, it is common for graduation ceremonies to take place at the end of the academic year, usually in May or June. It is recommended to check the university's official website or contact the university's registrar for the exact date and time of the graduation ceremony for Class of 2025.

### Question 44: How does the core quest course selection work to fulfill core credits?  
### Answer: 

The core quest course selection for Class of 2027 students and earlier consists of five core courses, each worth 4 credits. These core courses are Global Humanities, Modern Vietnamese Culture and Society, Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age, Scientific Inquiry, and Design and Systems Thinking. These courses total 20 credits.

Question: What are the Exploratory Requirements and how do they work?
Answer: The Exploratory Requirements encourage students to explore broad areas of study and discover their interests and passions. Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year.

### Question 45: Can I take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement?  
### Answer: 

No, according to the requirements, you should take six (06) 200-level intermediate courses and four (04) 300-level advanced courses. However, until the university offers a robust list of 200 and 300-Level Courses, you can satisfy the 48 Credits with any combination of 200 and 300 Level Courses. But it is recommended that you be guided by the above requirements when selecting courses where possible. Therefore, a 300-level course cannot be used to fulfill a 200-level major requirement.

### Question 46: If I take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn’t have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, can I count it toward that major?  
### Answer: 

No, if the course does not have a corresponding major code at Fulbright, it cannot be counted toward that major. However, you may still be eligible for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, but it would likely be applied to your Exploratory requirements or general electives, not your major requirements.

### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright as you need a minimum of 128 credit hours. You are currently short by 16 credits. The 16 credits from EL can count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval), but you still need to earn a total of 128 credit hours to graduate.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. ### Question 48: I have received an offer to attend an international conference but lack funding. What school funds can I apply for?  
### Answer: 

The school provides limited funding for materials and resources, including projects. However, the specific policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided. It is not clear if this funding can be used for attending international conferences, but you may want to discuss this with your academic/major advisor or the course instructor(s) to see if there are any available funds or resources that can help you attend the conference. Additionally, you may want to explore other funding opportunities, such as scholarships or grants, to help cover the costs of attending the conference.

8. Resources and Support: Available Resources Students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading. Funding and Material Procurement Projects will have access to limited funding for materials and resources. Policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided.

least 24 hours prior to class time. No permission will be granted on the day of the absence except in exceptional circumstances (see Section 11). Simply announcing an absence (for example, “I am going to miss tomorrow’s class”) does not constitute permission for an absence. • Discuss any unplanned absence or any known conflict with the course instructor(s) as soon as possible. • Make all late assignment submissions approved by the course instructor according to the instructions. • Contact the instructor to complete the Excused Absence form if having an absence due to participation in a sponsored academic event or being under exceptional circumstances applies. • Contact the Academic Affairs team or Registrar’s Office during business hours should you be unable to follow these instructions due to an emergency such as hospitalization following an accident. Fulbright is committed to supporting student learning when absences are unavoidable.

### Question 49: What is the maximum number of credits I can transfer from another university after officially enrolling at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

The maximum number of credits you can transfer from another university and credit to a Fulbright undergraduate degree is 64.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
their Fulbright undergraduate degree. This is referred to as Credit Transfer. In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar.

In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office. The request form must be approved and signed by the Academic/Major Advisor before submission. Students on a Leave of Absence (see Section 9) are considered to be still enrolled in the Fulbright undergraduate program during the period of the leave, though they are not registered for any courses. ### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can take only 2 courses as long as they meet the major or minor requirements and you maintain the full-time enrollment status of registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. However, your tuition fees will not be affected by taking only 2 courses, but if you withdraw from a course beyond the halfway point of that course, you will receive a grade of 'F' which may affect your GPA, and it may also affect your financial aid eligibility if it results in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

maintaining the full-time enrollment status of registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. • Course Withdrawal: There are two Withdrawal periods per term. The first period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4. During this time, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. Attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. ### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

Yes, if you have more than one major, the 8-credit limit for the Exploratory requirements is independently applied to each major. However, it is not specified in the context whether you can pursue more than three majors.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 58]
INTEGRATED SCIENCES: Description The Integrated Sciences major is a single, comprehensive program comprising a variety of fields, including Biology, Chemistry, and Environmental Science. Today’s most urgent scientific problems – from climate change to public health – require an integrated approach. Introducing multiple pathways in the natural science and emphasizing real-world experience, the Integrated Sciences major prepares students for careers as responsible and innovative scientific leaders and to seek interconnected solutions informed by several scientific disciplines. Students in the Integrated Sciences major will practice interdisciplinary and research-based approaches to scientific discovery, while also pursuing a specific concentration within the natural sciences: (1) Environmental Science and Sustainability, or (2) Biology and Health Science. The Integrated Sciences major provides a strong foundation for a career in industry as well as future graduate study. Learning Outcomes Students in the

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 58]

### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you would typically need to follow the process of declaring a major at your university. This usually involves meeting with an academic advisor in the department you wish to switch to, filling out a major declaration form, and submitting it to the appropriate office. However, the provided context does not mention any specific process for changing a major declaration. It only mentions the process for transferring credits and reducing course load, and the regulations for students on leave of absence.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

If you anticipate being unable to clear your account on time, you should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. After one term of Admin LOA, a student is officially withdrawn from Fulbright unless they have contacted the Registrar’s Office and confirmed the plan to return by registering for course(s) or have been granted a leave extension, a maximum of another term. The extension must be endorsed by the Registrar’s Office and approved by the Dean’s Office.

### Question 54: Which major has the fewest requirements?  
### Answer: 

The Class of 2023 is exempted from the Exploratory requirements, so they have no major requirements. For the other classes, the Class of 2023 students need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulfill their Exploratory requirements, while students of classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027 need to complete 32 credits (8 courses) to fulfill their Exploratory requirements. Therefore, the Class of 2023 has the fewest requirements.  

<details>

### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The number of courses a student can take depends on the specific requirements they are fulfilling. For major or minor requirements, a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) can be double-counted. For exploratory requirements, students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses) from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. There is no limit mentioned on the total number of courses a student can take. However, students are encouraged to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

### Question 56: How many courses in a semester can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The number of courses a student can take in a semester is not explicitly stated in the context. However, it is mentioned that students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. This suggests that a student can take up to 4 courses in a semester if they are not double-counting credits. If a student is double-counting credits, they can take up to 6 courses in a semester. The number of courses a student can take in a semester may also depend on the university's policies regarding course load.

### Question 58: How can I audit a course?  
### Answer: 

The text does not provide information on how to audit a course. However, it does mention that students can apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, which might involve auditing a course as a prerequisite. To find out the process for auditing a course, students should refer to their institution's academic policies or contact the Office of the Registrar or the Office of the Dean.

courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

If two majors share cross-listed or tagged courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged.

• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. ### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

The grade points are assigned to letter grades according to the following scale:

Letter Grade Grade Point
A 4.0
A- 3.7
B+ 3.3
B 3.0
B- 2.7
C+ 2.3
C 2.0
C- 1.7
D+ 1.3
D 1.0
D- 0.7
F 0.0

The grade category percentage is also provided in the context.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
GRADING: At Fulbright, the majority of courses apply a standard letter grade ranging from ‘A’ to ‘F.’ Grade points are assigned to letter grades according to the following scale (unless otherwise decided by faculty in individual courses): Letter Grade Grade Point Grade Category Percentage

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
GRADING: At Fulbright, the majority of courses apply a standard letter grade ranging from ‘A’ to ‘F.’ Grade points are assigned to letter grades according to the following scale (unless otherwise decided by faculty in individual courses): Letter Grade Grade Point Grade Category Percentage

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
The final grade for the thesis is the average of the 2 graders. The oral defense is graded by a panel of all IS faculty. See Appendix 1and 2 for detail rubrics on both the thesis and presentation. The total grade of the capstone is the sum of the thesis grade and oral defense grade. The primary advisor will communicate this result and any feedback from the graders to the student in writing. If there are any concerns about the grades, students should first meet with their primary advisor to discuss and clarify. If no agreement is made, the student could request one more grader (an IS faculty) to grade their submission, but cannot choose who the grader would be. The major coordinator will decide the 3rd grader after discussion with IS faculty team. The new grade would be the average of the 3 graders. Any further appeal after this would need to follow official UG program’s process for grade appeal.

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]

The total grade of the capstone is the sum of the thesis grade and oral defense grade. The primary advisor will communicate this result and any feedback from the graders to the student in writing. If no agreement is made, the student could request one more grader (an IS faculty) to grade their submission, but cannot choose who the grader would be. The major coordinator will decide the 3rd grader after discussion with IS faculty team. The new grade would be the average of the 3 graders. Any further appeal after this would need to follow official UG program’s process for grade appeal.

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 36]
[F09 – RO/FUV]: Review of Final Grade Request If you have discussed your concerns with your instructor(s) and you are not satisfied, you may request a formal review of your final grade. You may not challenge a final course grade on the basis of an individual in-course piece of work that has or has not previously been re- marked. A request to review a final grade will normally be premised on a miscalculation of the final grade or deviation from the evaluation procedures described in the course outline. This request form shall be submitted to the Office of the Registrar within five (05) working days from the final grade released date. ### Question 61: What grade is A in scale of 4?  
### Answer: 

A in the given scale corresponds to 4.0, which is the highest grade.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You may get academic suspension if you fail to meet all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The suspension is entered on your transcript as part of your academic record. You must meet with the Dean's Office, who will establish the conditions you must meet prior to returning to Fulbright. While on suspension, you may not visit the Fulbright campus unless permission is given from the Dean's Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions typically last for one term or one academic year. You may be suspended a maximum of two times. If you are suspended a third time, your enrolment in the program will be canceled, and you will have to apply for re-admission. Your re-admission decision will be made by the Dean's Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. If re-admitted, you will also have to re-apply for financial aid.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]

It is intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). Students on Academic Warning who fail to meet all the requirements of their Learning Contract may require an additional Academic Progress Meeting and may be placed on Academic Probation, typically resulting in an updated Learning Contract. ### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP grade is an option for students to take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year. To do this, they need to complete a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submit it to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term. The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the grade to P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. It's important to note that once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. Also, Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.  

<details>

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 2 courses, 4 credits each, on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year. However, Pass/No Pass grades do not contribute to the official transcript GPA. Only a grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses, but they do not count towards the GPA. Courses with a No Pass grade will not be counted towards any requirements and will be shown on the Official Transcript with an NP grade.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

Yes, the failed grade will count toward the total attempted credits, but it will not be included in the GPA calculation as it will be overwritten by the notation "RP". However, the repeated course will not count toward the 144 maximum credits you can have if you retake it and pass it. It's important to consult with your Academic/Major Advisor about your program plan if you are considering taking the class for a third time.
