### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. To receive an Academic Warning, a student will be sent a notice by the Registrar's Office. The student is then required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

ACADEMIC STANDING: Academic standing refers to how well a Fulbright student is meeting the general expectations toward the fulfillment of their degree. There are four categories of academic standing. 6.1 Good Standing Students with a minimum of 2.0 GPA, who are not on academic or non- academic warning, probation, suspension, or dismissal, and who are in good standing financially, are considered in Good Standing. Only students in Good Standing may participate in off-campus programs and other opportunities as specified. 6.2 Academic Warning This is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. ### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, you would need to take a combination of Pure Mathematics, Intermediate, Advanced, and Elective Applied courses. Here are some examples:

Pure Mathematics:
- Abstract Algebra
- Real Analysis

Intermediate Courses:
- Probability
- Differential Equations
- Discrete Mathematics
- Numerical Analysis

Advanced Courses:
- Advanced Statistics
- Statistical Learning
- Stochastic Calculus
- Numerical Analysis
- Optimization
- Partial Differential Equations

Elective Applied Courses (at least one at 200 level):
- Game theory (Economics)
- The Economics of Corruption (Economics)
- Money and Banking (Economics)
- Economics of Inequality (Economics)

You will also need to take at least 2 additional advanced courses from the areas of Applied Statistics, Engineering Mathematics, or Data Science, after consulting with an academic advisor.

Additionally, you will need to complete Multivariable Calculus and at least 1 Intermediate course. A Capstone project (optional) and Research seminars are also available. It's recommended to consult with an academic advisor for course selection and to ensure you meet all the requirements for declaring the Applied Mathematics major.

### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To formally declare Computer Science as their major, a student must complete at least two Computer Science courses. These can include MATH 202: Discrete Math, CS 101: Introduction to Programming, CS 201: Data Structures & Algorithms, CS 203: Computer Organization, and any three intermediate courses, CS 302: Algorithms & Theory of Computing, and four advanced courses. Additionally, the student must complete Capstone I and Capstone II, or an additional intermediate course or an advanced course in each of these slots.

### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

The Experiential Learning Program (ELP) at Fulbright University requires students to complete a minimum of 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits as a graduation requirement. However, the program is designed for students to gain academic credit through experiential learning experiences, which typically involve some form of compensation. Since you're not being paid by the company, it seems you're in an exceptional circumstance. To get the subsidy, you would need to submit a petition to the Registrar's Office, along with supporting documentation and the authorization of the course instructor, your academic/major advisor, and the Registrar's Office. The tuition credit, if approved, will follow the "Fees & Charges Guide" for undergraduate students. Keep in mind that no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits, and course withdrawals may affect your financial aid eligibility if they result in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. For more details, please refer to the Experiential Learning Program section on the Fulbright One Stop portal.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours.  The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office. The request form must be approved and signed by the Academic/Major Advisor before submission. Students on a Leave of Absence (see Section 9) are considered to be still enrolled in the Fulbright undergraduate program during the period of the leave, though they are not registered for any courses. ### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The process of making a Capstone for graduation in the context provided involves the following steps:

1. Identify your area of interest and decide on the format of your Capstone (thesis, art work, film, etc.). Consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project.

2. Begin the initial stages of production (subject to your advisors’ approval).

3. In Capstone I, you will work with your primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. You will meet with your advisor as early as possible and set a regular meeting schedule and expectations for submissions with timeline. The end-of-term submission will demonstrate successful progress towards the final Capstone submission, and satisfactory completion. This submission may include a literature review or annotated bibliography of at least five pages, an introduction, and other materials/documents to be decided on in consultation with your advisors.

4. In Capstone II, you will focus more on production, whether it be writing your thesis or realizing a creative project. The Capstone culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II. It culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers. Students work with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. The format and length of projects is flexible, within certain limits. This handbook explains each aspect of the Capstone experience so that you can plan ahead and know what to expect. 1.2. ### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

The question does not provide information about any distinctive graduation requirements related to grades. However, it is mentioned that a grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. This suggests that a student needs to pass their courses with a grade of 'C-' or higher to progress in their studies, but it does not specify any distinctive graduation requirements.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with Honor, you need to earn an honor pass in the Capstone. The final grade of the Capstone is on a Pass/No pass/Honor basis. An honor pass is given if you score 90 to 100 points. To earn an honor pass, you should focus on the grading rubric in Appendix 1 for the written thesis and Appendix 2 for the presentation. The Capstone is worth 100 points, with 85 points for the thesis and 15 points for the presentation.

Additionally, to maintain a GPA high enough to graduate with Honor, you should aim to achieve a GPA of 3.6 or higher throughout your senior year. If you fail to maintain the required GPA, your Capstone will be capped at Pass.

Lastly, it's important to note that all courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. So, it's crucial to complete your work on time and avoid withdrawals or incomplete grades if you want to maximize your GPA.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 2 courses, each with 4 credits, on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year.

Question: What is the minimum grade to earn credit for a course?
Answer: A grade of 'D' is the minimum grade to earn credit for a course.

Question: What is the minimum grade to pass a course taken on Pass/No Pass basis?
Answer: A minimum grade of 'C-' is required to pass a course taken on Pass/No Pass basis.

Question: Can I use Pass/No Pass grades to count toward major/minor requirements?
Answer: No, Pass/No Pass grades cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

Question: Can I use Pass/No Pass grades to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses?
Answer: Yes, courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

Question: What happens if I get a grade below 'C-' in a course taken on Pass/No Pass basis?
Answer: If you get a grade below 'C-' in a course taken on Pass/No Pass basis, you will receive a No Pass grade, and no credit will be granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

Question: What is the maximum time to complete unfinished course work for an Incomplete grade?
Answer: The student has until the date agreed upon with the faculty (not to exceed 6 months from the end of the course) to complete all remaining course work for an Incomplete grade.

Question: What is the minimum grade required to pass a course and be counted toward major/minor requirements or to be used to fulfill a prerequisite to register for more advanced courses?
Answer: A minimum grade of 'C-' is required to pass a course and be counted toward major/minor requirements or to be used to fulfill a prerequisite to register for more advanced courses.

Question: Can Pass/No Pass grades be used to count toward elective courses?
Answer: Yes, grades 'D' or 'D+' can only be counted toward the requirements for elective courses.

Question: Can Pass/No Pass grades be used to count toward core courses?
Answer: No, Pass/No Pass grades cannot be used to count toward core courses.

Question: Can I change the grade option from Pass/No Pass back to a letter grade after converting it?
Answer: Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back.

Question: What is the deadline to submit the Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form?
Answer: The deadline to submit the Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form is 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term (16-week term).

Question: What happens to the grade after the Registrar’s Office converts it to P/NP?
Answer: The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the final grade to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term.

Question: What is the grade point value for a Pass grade?
Answer: The grade point value for a Pass grade is not specified in the provided context.

Question: What is the grade point value for a No Pass grade?
Answer: The grade point value for a No Pass grade is not specified in the provided context.

Question: Can I use Pass/No Pass grades to count toward the total credits required for graduation?
Answer: The provided context does not specify whether Pass/No Pass grades can be used to count toward the total credits required for graduation.

Question: Can I use Pass/No Pass grades to count toward the GPA calculation?
Answer: The provided context does not specify whether Pass/No Pass grades can be used to count toward the GPA calculation.

Question: Can I use Pass/No Pass grades to count toward the requirements for a scholarship or financial aid?
Answer: The provided context does not specify whether Pass/No Pass grades can be used to count toward the requirements for a scholarship or financial aid.

### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of absences: general absences, military leave, and excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence at Fulbright: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have a leave of absence, a student must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, along with supporting documents, before the last day of class. For a Medical Leave, the student must also submit the Fulbright Impact Assessment form and all medical supporting documents. The specific requirements and procedures may vary depending on the type of leave.

LEAVE OF ABSENCE: Students who wish to take a period of leave from their studies at Fulbright must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form , along with supporting documents, before the last day of class. Fulbright permits students in Good Academic Standing to apply for a leave of absence for one to two terms. Normally, a student is not permitted to remain on campus during a period of absence from their studies. Students may return earlier to Fulbright by notifying the Registrar’s Office at least eight (08) weeks in advance of the returning term. Students who return and resume their studies at Fulbright are expected to complete their program without further interruption. The effective date of the Leave of Absence will be from the date of request submission if it’s approved. mission if it’s approved. ### Question 77: How can I report violation of Academic environment anonymously?  
### Answer: 

The context does not provide information on how to report violations of academic environment anonymously. However, it mentions that Academic Integrity is one of the reasons for Academic Warning, which could include academic dishonesty. If a student suspects academic dishonesty, they can report it to the Academic Integrity Office, but it is not specified whether anonymous reporting is possible. It is recommended to check the university's policies or contact the university administration for more information on anonymous reporting.

An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. ### Question 78: Where can I get all forms and pdf related to my academic journey at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

You can find all forms and PDFs related to your academic journey at Fulbright on the Fulbright One Stop portal. These include the Incomplete Grade Request form, the Exit Checklist with Academic Affairs, the Exit Checklist with Residential Life, and the Transcript of Records. Additionally, you may need to submit proof of your attendance at any activities or programs you will be attending during your absence, as well as proof of your travel.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is not explicitly mentioned in the provided context. However, it is implied that academic integrity issues could be a reason for an Academic Warning, Academic Probation, or Academic Suspension. These interventions are typically for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree, have a GPA below 2.0, or have issues with attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. The specifics of how academic dishonesty is handled are not detailed in the provided context.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

Students are required to repeat core courses if they receive a grade of F or if the course is counted towards their major/minor and they receive a grade below 'C-'. They may also repeat a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP', or have withdrawn and received a grade of 'W'. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with their academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. Students may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed. If a student wishes to dispute a final grade, they should first discuss the matter with the course instructor. If the matter remains unresolved, they may file an appeal within five business days from the date the final grade is posted. The appeal process involves the Registrar's Office, the Dean's Office, and a potential panel review for an independent evaluation of the grade. The final grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade.

In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a ‘D+’ following consultation with the student’s academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. ### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance by considering them under the category of exceptional circumstances. This includes exceptional medical circumstances, close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties, legal proceedings, and emergency situations. In these cases, students are responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. For trips during the term, the approval of the Office of the Dean and Deans of Students must be obtained. Students should be in good academic standing and not on probation to be excused from the class. The faculty or supervising staff is responsible for checking the student's academic standing with the Registrar's Office before approving the excused absence form. If a student must miss class(es) for a university-sponsored event, the faculty or staff responsible for that event requests a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form and submits it to the Dean’s Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office in cc for the record. Only faculty or supervising staff can request the Excused Absence for students.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided context, the use of generative AI like ChatGPT is allowed in academic projects at Fulbright University Vietnam, but it is subject to the regulations described in the Code of Academic Integrity. Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include details about the objective and scope, tools and platforms, process and methodology, and ethical and copyright issues associated with using generative AI. It is important to note that presenting text, images, or other content created by generative AI or others as your own work is grounds for failure of Capstone I and/or Capstone II. Therefore, students should be careful to properly cite and attribute any AI-generated content they use in their assignments.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer:

Additionally, there are resources available like a Mental Health First Aid Training Program, a Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, a Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services, and possibly therapeutic gardening or nature programs.

### Question 87: Where can I get the assist for internship?  
### Answer: 

The resources and support provided for the students include industry mentors who may be available for project guidance. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading. However, it is not specified that they can assist with internships. You should consult with your primary advisor or the department's internship coordinator for assistance with internships.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: HCE_Capstone_Handbook_Final_2025.01.16.pdf, Page: 9]
8. Resources and Support: Available Resources Students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work. Support will be provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary. Mentorship and Industry Involvement Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading. Funding and Material Procurement Projects will have access to limited funding for materials and resources. Policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

The information about university-sponsored events and activities that might interrupt your study time is not directly provided in the context. However, it is mentioned that if a student must miss class(es) for a university-sponsored event, the faculty or staff responsible for that event requests a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form and submits it to the Dean’s Office. You could potentially reach out to the Dean’s Office or the Office of the Deans of Students to inquire about upcoming events that might affect your study schedule. Additionally, you could also check the university's calendar of events or bulletin boards for announcements about events happening on campus.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit from another university to Fulbright University Vietnam, you should submit an Application for Credit Transfer to the Office of the Registrar. In the application, you should provide all the information requested about the course(s) for which you are applying to transfer, including course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit is justified. For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal. You should also send an official transcript with seal from the issuing institution directly to the Office of the Registrar at the email registrar@fulbright.edu.vn or the mailing address in the Policy.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
their Fulbright undergraduate degree. This is referred to as Credit Transfer. In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The Capstone by Applied Project (CWP) requires students to conduct a critical literature review and design their project using the Creswell & Creswell textbook as a foundation. The final submission will be in the form of a critical evaluation report. The Capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and primary research is encouraged. However, it should not require extensive fieldwork. The scope of research and production for the Capstone should be carefully considered, and students are advised to consult with their advisor early on. Applications which do not demonstrate awareness of the scope and practicalities needed to realize the Capstone may not be approved. The Capstone panel, which includes the advisor(s), will evaluate the final reports and public presentations using a rubric with equal weight for each criterion. The final scores are computed with a weight distribution of 40% for the advisor(s), 30% for the independent reviewer, and 30% for the capstone panel. In exceptional cases, the capstone project can be evaluated as Pass with Honor, otherwise it will be Pass. The Pass grade is equivalent to at least 70% to 89.9% of the final scores, and the Pass with Honor grade is equivalent to at least 90% of the final scores.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Psychology Capstone Handbook 2025-2026.pdf, Page: 6]
a critical Literature Review, and a Method. Creswell, J. & Creswell, D. (2022). Research design: Qualitative, quantitative, and mixed methods approaches (6th ed). Sage. Capstone by Applied Project For the Applied Project stream, your advisor will also provide resources that are relevant to the fundamentals of your Applied Project.  The above Creswell & Creswell textbook also serves as a foundation for the literature review, theoretical foundation, and design of your Applied Project. Since the final submission will be in the form of a critical evaluation report, we additionally highly recommend the following textbook for background in program evaluation: Russ-Eft, D., & Preskill, H. (2009). Evaluation in organizations: A systematic approach to enhancing learning, performance, and change, 2nd ed. Basic Books. Your supervisor will work with you to identify learning resources for Capstone 2. This will depend on the nature and progression of your project.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you may be exempt from some physical education courses required to graduate. However, the specifics would depend on the university's policies. You should consult with your athletic department and academic advisor to understand the exact requirements and any necessary procedures for exemption.

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

To register for university dormitory again, you would need to submit a request to the Residential Life staff. However, your financial support may not be guaranteed as it is typically provided during the first year. You should also be aware that if you move back into the dormitory, you will be subject to the dormitory's rules and regulations, and you will be required to pay any outstanding balances or fees for damages to your previous room. Additionally, if you are facing financial difficulties, you should meet with the Student Financial Services team to discuss alternative solutions and request a late and/or extension of tuition fee payment. If you withdraw from the university in the middle of the academic year, you should submit an official letter to the Office of the Registrar.

With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. After one term of Admin LOA, a student is

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 36]

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

To request for funds to support club activities, students can apply for funding from FUV. FUV has a student research fund which supports student’s research projects, including capstone. The process might involve significant paperwork, such as application of funding, disbursements of fund, and getting approval for the use of the funds. It is crucial that you complete this process as soon as possible.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are several ways provided by the university to support students in their academic path. These include:

1. Access to labs, tools, and software relevant to project work.
2. Support for learning new software or techniques where necessary.
3. Mentorship and Industry Involvement: Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel.
4. Funding and Material Procurement: Projects will have access to limited funding for materials and resources. Policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided.
5. Exploratory Requirements: Students are required to complete a certain number of credits in different categories to discover their interests and passions. Up to two exploratory credits can be counted towards the student’s major requirements.
6. Student Research Fund: FUV has a student research fund which supports student’s research projects, including capstone.
7. Assistance in securing resources: If certain materials, equipment, or samples are not available, the university can help students find other institutions where they could access the needed resources, or students can apply for funding to purchase the necessary items. If there is no viable way to get access to the equipment, changes to the experimental design might be necessary. Students should discuss with their advisors.

<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: HCE_Capstone_Handbook_Final_2025.01.16.pdf, Page: 9]

Support will be provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary. Mentorship and Industry Involvement Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading. Funding and Material Procurement Projects will have access to limited funding for materials and resources. Policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided.

and discover more fully where their interests and passions lie. Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulﬁll more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. ### Question 95: Can you give me the information about student fees and charges policy?  
### Answer: 

The fees and charges policy for undergraduate students at Fulbright University can be found in the "Fees & Charges Guide". However, tuition credit will be considered for students who experience exceptional circumstances that impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, as long as they provide supporting documentation and receive authorization from their course instructor(s), academic/major advisor, and the Registrar's Office. It's important to note that no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits, and course withdrawals may affect financial aid eligibility if they result in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment.

EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

If you believe there has been an issue with the teaching methods of a professor, you should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the issue remains unresolved, you may file an appeal by submitting the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. The Registrar's Office will then inform the Dean’s Office of the case, and if necessary, organize a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the situation. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter. It is important to remember to correspond professionally and courteously throughout the process.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Art & Media Studies Capstone Handbook _v3_210125.pdf, Page: 6]
progress, and as such, will be the person with whom you meet most frequently. The secondary advisor can offer you additional feedback where necessary and may represent a disciplinary field outside of Art & Media Studies (if your project is interdisciplinary). In some cases where the primary advisor is unable to continue, the secondary advisor will assume their role. You should plan to meet with your primary advisor at least once a month during the semester, if not more often. You should also plan to meet with your secondary advisor before important deadlines of the semester if not more often. You are expected to initiate these meetings with your advisors. The capstone places responsibility on you to be organized and to be responsible in regular communications and submission of work-in-progression to your primary and secondary advisors. Failure to do this will result in the capping of your final submission at Pass. REMEMBER: ü Respect your advisors’ working hours ü Correspond professionally and courteously ü

APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

You can seek advice from your academic advisor or the faculty members who taught the research seminars you have completed. They can help you understand the benefits and requirements of a Capstone project and guide you in making a decision based on your interests and post-graduation plans. If you're unsure about the topic or need expert guidance, you may also consider requesting an external secondary advisor who specializes in your chosen subject. The History Capstone Handbook, AY2025-26 can also provide you with more information about the Capstone experience.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II. It culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers. Students work with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. The format and length of projects is flexible, within certain limits. This handbook explains each aspect of the Capstone experience so that you can plan ahead and know what to expect. 1.2. History Capstone Learning Outcomes Students who successfully complete a Capstone project will be able to: 1. Demonstrate

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
Your primary advisor may not be an expert on your chosen subject and almost certainly isn’t an expert on the narrow historical problem you will tackle in your Capstone project—and that is okay! The main role of your Capstone advisor is to guide you through the research process and to evaluate your mastery of that process, regardless of the topic. If you feel that you need expert guidance on a particular topic and that no one on our faculty has specialized knowledge on that topic, you may want to consider requesting an external secondary advisor who does. Another way to approach this is to propose a Capstone project based on a 300-level research seminar that you have taken at Fulbright, or to ask the faculty for topic suggestions—that way, you are more likely to end up with a primary advisor who is also a subject-matter expert! [Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
Your primary advisor may not be an expert on your chosen subject and almost certainly isn’t an expert on the narrow historical problem you will tackle in your Capstone project—and that is okay! The main role of your Capstone advisor is to guide you through the research process and to evaluate your mastery of that process, regardless of the topic. [Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and  

</details> 

### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

To attend the tournament with the Fulbright Basketball Club, you should first discuss your absence with your course instructors as soon as possible. If your absence is due to participation in a sponsored academic event, you will need to complete the Excused Absence form. To get the official transcript, you should contact the Registrar's Office during business hours. After the tournament, you will also need to write a reflection paper about your experience and submit it to ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn.

least 24 hours prior to class time. No permission will be granted on the day of the absence except in exceptional circumstances (see Section 11). Fulbright is committed to supporting student learning when absences are unavoidable.

### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

To borrow books from the library, you will need to have a library card. You can obtain a library card by visiting the library and providing identification. Once you have a library card, you can search the library's catalog online or in person to find the books you want to borrow. When you find a book you want to borrow, you can place a hold on it, or you can go to the library and check it out at the circulation desk. The library will have specific rules about how long you can keep the book, and you may be charged fines if you do not return it on time. When you are finished with the book, you can return it to the library at any time. If you are unable to return the book on time, you can renew it online or by contacting the library.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work with the major report, you should follow the guidelines provided in the Evaluation Report. This includes writing an Executive Summary that outlines the project's purpose, objectives, methods, and anticipated impact. The Rationale should explain the theoretical and psychological foundations for the project, detailing its objectives and significance. These sections should be clear, concise, and effectively communicate the project's goals and their relevance to the field of psychology or applied mental health. Additionally, remember to apply psychological principles to behavioral phenomena, interpret, design, and conduct basic psychological research, incorporate sociocultural factors in scientific inquiry when appropriate, and apply ethical standards to evaluate and engage in psychological science and practice, as these are the Major Learning Outcomes for the Psychology Major.

Outcomes Students who have completed the Psychology Major will have achieved the following Learning Outcomes: 1. ### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

The number of elective credits may vary, so there are multiple ways to fill in the requirements of EL. However, the total number of earned credits must be enough to complete the degree. For Class of 2024 students, they need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) for their Exploratory requirements, and the remaining credits can be filled with electives. For Class of 2025, 2026, and 2027 students, they need to complete 32 credits (8 courses) for their Exploratory requirements, and the remaining credits can be filled with electives. The number of elective credits needed will depend on the total number of credits required to complete the degree.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and passions lie. Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year.
